Negative if expired.\"\"\"\r\n        return int(self.exp - time.time())\r\n\r\n    def to_dict(self) -> dict[str, Any]:\r\n        return {\r\n            \"sub\": self.sub,\r\n            \"typ\": self.typ,\r\n            \"iat\": self.iat,\r\n            \"exp\": self.exp,\r\n            \"jti\": self.jti,\r\n            \"iss\": self.iss,\r\n            \"roles\": self.roles,\r\n            \"permissions\": self.permissions,\r\n            \"metadata\": self.metadata,\r\n        }\r\n\r\n\r\nclass JWTManager:\r\n    \"\"\"\r\n    Handles JWT token creation and validation using HMAC-SHA256.\r\n\r\n    This is a lightweight implementation that doesn't depend on PyJWT\r\n    for core operations, making it suitable for embedded use.\r\n    \"\"\"\r\n\r\n    def __init__(\r\n        self,\r\n        secret_key: str,\r\n        algorithm: str = \"HS256\",\r\n        issuer: str = \"nexusflow\",\r\n        access_ttl: int = 3600,\r\n        refresh_ttl: int = 86400,\r\n        clock_skew_tolerance: int = 30,\r\n    ) -> None:\r\n        if not secret_key:\r\n            raise ValueError(\"JWT secret_key cannot be empty\")\r\n\r\n        self._secret_key = secret_key\r\n        self._algorithm = algorithm\r\n        self._issuer = issuer\r\n        self._access_ttl = access_ttl\r\n        self._refresh_ttl = refresh_ttl\r\n        self._clock_skew = clock_skew_tolerance\r\n\r\n        # Map of revoked JTIs to their expiration time\r\n        self._revoked: dict[str, int] = {}\r\n\r\n    def create_token(\r\n        self,\r\n        user_id: str,\r\n        token_type: TokenType = TokenType.ACCESS,\r\n        roles: Optional[list[str]] = None,\r\n        permissions: Optional[list[str]] = None,\r\n        metadata: Optional[dict[str, Any]] = None,\r\n        custom_ttl: Optional[int] = None,\r\n    ) -> str:\r\n        \"\"\"\r\n        Create a signed JWT token.\r\n\r\n        BUG CANDIDATE #1: The JTI (JWT ID) is generated using a hash of\r\n        user_id + current timestamp. When two tokens are created for the\r\n        same user within the same second, they get the same JTI. This\r\n        means revoking one revokes both.\r\n        \"\"\"\r\n        now = int(time.time())\r\n\r\n        if custom_ttl is not None:\r\n            ttl = custom_ttl\r\n        elif token_type == TokenType.REFRESH:\r\n            ttl = self._refresh_ttl\r\n        else:\r\n            ttl = self._access_ttl\r\n\r\n        # Generate JTI — unique token identifier\r\n        jti_input = f\"{user_id}:{now}:{token_type.value}\"\r\n        jti = hashlib.sha256(jti_input.encode()).hexdigest()[:16]\r\n\r\n        claims = TokenClaims(\r\n            sub=user_id,\r\n            typ=token_type.value,\r\n            iat=now,\r\n            exp=now + ttl,\r\n            jti=jti,\r\n            iss=self._issuer,\r\n            roles=roles or [],\r\n            permissions=permissions or [],\r\n            metadata=metadata or {},\r\n        )\r\n\r\n        return self._encode(claims)\r\n\r\n    def validate_token(self, token: str) -> TokenClaims:\r\n        \"\"\"\r\n        Validate and decode a JWT token.\r\n\r\n        BUG CANDIDATE #1: The clock skew tolerance is applied asymmetrically.\r\n        For expiration, we check `exp + clock_skew > now` (allowing tokens\r\n        to remain valid slightly past their exp). But for `iat` (issued-at),\r\n        we check `iat > now + clock_skew` to reject future-dated tokens.\r\n\r\n        The subtle bug: when the clock_skew_tolerance is large and a token's\r\n        exp falls exactly at `now`, the comparison `now > exp` is True (expired),\r\n        but `now > exp + clock_skew` is False (still valid). This inconsistency\r\n        means the is_expired property on TokenClaims (which doesn't account for\r\n        skew) disagrees with validate_token.\r\n        \"\"\"\r\n        claims = self._decode(token)\r\n\r\n        # Check issuer\r\n        if claims.iss != self._issuer:\r\n            raise TokenInvalidError(f\"Invalid issuer: expected '{self._issuer}', got '{claims.iss}'\")\r\n\r\n        # Check expiration with clock skew tolerance\r\n        now = int(time.time())\r\n        if now > claims.exp + self._clock_skew:\r\n            raise TokenExpiredError(\r\n                f\"Token expired at {claims.exp}, current time is {now} \"\r\n                f\"(tolerance: {self._clock_skew}s)\"\r\n            )\r\n\r\n        # Check not-before (iat shouldn't be too far in the future)\r\n        if claims.iat > now + self._clock_skew:\r\n            raise TokenInvalidError(\r\n                f\"Token issued in the future: iat={claims.iat}, now={now}\"\r\n            )\r\n\r\n        # Check revocation\r\n        if claims.jti in self._revoked:\r\n            raise TokenInvalidError(f\"Token has been revoked (jti={claims.jti})\")\r\n\r\n        return claims\r\n\r\n    def revoke_token(self, token_or_jti: str) -> None:\r\n        \"\"\"Revoke a token by its JTI or by the full token string.\"\"\"\r\n        if \".\" in token_or_jti:\r\n            # It's a full token, decode to get JTI\r\n            claims = self._decode(token_or_jti)\r\n            jti = claims.jti\r\n            exp = claims.exp\r\n        else:\r\n            jti = token_or_jti\r\n            exp = int(time.time()) + self._access_ttl  # Assume access token TTL\r\n\r\n        self._revoked[jti] = exp\r\n\r\n    def cleanup_revoked(self) -> int:\r\n        \"\"\"Remove expired entries from the revocation list. Returns count removed.\"\"\"\r\n        now = int(time.time())\r\n        expired_jtis = [jti for jti, exp in self._revoked.items() if exp < now]\r\n        for jti in expired_jtis:\r\n            del self._revoked[jti]\r\n        return len(expired_jtis)\r\n\r\n    def refresh_token(self, refresh_token: str) -> tuple[str, str]:\r\n        \"\"\"\r\n        Use a refresh token to generate a new access + refresh token pair.\r\n\r\n        BUG CANDIDATE #12: Race condition — if two threads call refresh_token\r\n        with the same refresh token simultaneously, both may succeed before\r\n        the old token is revoked, producing two valid access tokens.\r\n        The revocation of the old refresh token happens AFTER the new tokens\r\n        are created, leaving a window.\r\n        \"\"\"\r\n        claims = self.validate_token(refresh_token)\r\n\r\n        if claims.token_type != TokenType.REFRESH:\r\n            raise TokenInvalidError(\"Cannot refresh with a non-refresh token\")\r\n\r\n        # user_id: str,\r\n        resource: str,\r\n        action: Action,\r\n        raise_on_deny: bool = True,\r\n    ) -> bool:\r\n        \"\"\"\r\n        Check if a user has permission to perform an before.\r\n        This means a cycle A->B->A will recurse once before being caught.\r\n        For small cycles this wastes work; for larger cycles with side effects\r\n        it could cause incorrect permission accumulation.\r\n        \"\"\"\r\n        role = self._roles.get(role_name)\r\n        if role is None:\r\n            logger.warning(f\"Role '{role_name}' not found during resolution\")\r\n            return set()\r\n\r\n        perms = role.permissions.copy()\r\n\r\n        # Add parent role permissions\r\n        for parent_name in role.parent_roles:\r\n            if parent_name in visited:\r\n                logger.warning(f\"Circular role inheritance detected: {parent_name}\")\r\n                continue\r\n            visited.add(role_name)\r\n            parent_perms = self._resolve_role_permissions(parent_name, visited)\r\n            perms.update(parent_perms)\r\n\r\n        return perms\r\n\r\n    def get_effective_permissions(self, user_id: str) -> list[dict[str, str]]:\r\n        \"\"\"Get a human-readable list of effective permissions for a user.\"\"\"\r\n        perms = self._resolve_user_permissions(user_id)\r\n        return [\r\n            {\"resource\": p.resource, \"action\": p.action.value}\r\n            for p in sorted(perms, key=lambda p: (p.resource, p.action.value))\r\n        ]\r\n","exit_code":0,"status":"completed"}}

self.created_at) > self.ttl\r\n\r\n    @property\r\n    def age(self) -> float:\r\n        \"\"\"Return the age of this entry in seconds.\"\"\"\r\n        return time.time() - self.created_at\r\n\r\n    def touch(self) -> None:\r\n        \"\"\"Update access metadata.\"\"\"\r\n        self.access_count += 1\r\n        self.last_accessed = time.time()\r\n\r\n\r\nclass CacheStats:\r\n    \"\"\"Track cache hit/miss statistics.\"\"\"\r\n\r\n    def __init__(self) -> None:\r\n        self.hits: int = 0\r\n        self.misses: int = 0\r\n        self.evictions: int = 0\r\n        self.invalidations: int = 0\r\n        self.expirations: int = 0\r\n\r\n    @property\r\n    def hit_rate(self) -> float:\r\n        total = self.hits + self.misses\r\n        if total == 0:\r\n            return 0.0\r\n        return self.hits / total\r\n\r\n    def to_dict(self) -> Dict[str, Any]:\r\n        return {\r\n            \"hits\": self.hits,\r\n            \"misses\": self.misses,\r\n            \"evictions\": self.evictions,\r\n            \"invalidations\": self.invalidations,\r\n            \"expirations\": self.expirations,\r\n            \"hit_rate\": round(self.hit_rate, 4),\r\n        }\r\n\r\n    def reset(self) -> None:\r\n        self.hits = 0\r\n        self.misses = 0\r\n        self.evictions = 0\r\n        self.invalidations = 0\r\n        self.expirations = 0\r\n\r\n\r\nclass QueryCache:\r\n    \"\"\"\r\n    LRU cache with TTL for query results.\r\n\r\n    Supports cache tags for group invalidation and integrates\r\n    with the transaction system.\r\n\r\n    BUG CANDIDATE #4: When a query is executed inside a transaction\r\n    and the result is cached, rolling back that transaction does NOT\r\n    invalidate the cached result. Subsequent reads will get stale data.\r\n    \"\"\"\r\n\r\n    def __init__(\r\n        self,\r\n        max_size: int = 1000,\r\n        default_ttl: float = 300.0,\r\n    ) -> None:\r\n        self._max_size = max_size\r\n        self._default_ttl = default_ttl\r\n        self._cache: OrderedDict[str, CacheEntry] = OrderedDict()\r\n        self._tag_index: Dict[str, Set[str]] = {}\r\n        self._stats = CacheStats()\r\n        self._lock = threading.RLock()\r\n        self._invalidation_callbacks: List[Callable[[str], None]] = []\r\n        # The entry is stored normally and will survive\r\n        a transaction rollback.\r\n        \"\"\"\r\n        key = self._make_key(query, params)\r\n        effective_ttl = ttl if ttl is not None else self._default_ttl\r\n        entry_tags = tags or set()\r\n\r\n        with self._lock:\r\n            # Evict if at capacity\r\n            while len(self._cache) >= self._max_size:\r\n                self._evict_one()\r\n\r\n            entry = CacheEntry(\r\n                key=key,\r\n                value=result,\r\n                created_at=time.time(),\r\n                ttl=effective_ttl,\r\n                tags=entry_tags,\r\n                transaction_id=transaction_id,\r\n            )\r\n            self._cache[key] = entry\r\n            self._cache.move_to_end(key)\r\n\r\n            # Update tag index\r\n            for tag in entry_tags:\r\n                if tag not in self._tag_index:\r\n                    self._tag_index[tag] = set()\r\n                self._tag_index[tag].add(key)\r\n\r\n            # BUG: We store the transaction_id but never register it\r\n            # for rollback tracking.
